class="mergedbottomrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Density</div></th><td>560/km<sup>2</sup> (1,450.4/sq&#160;mi)&#32;(<a of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">66th</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>&#160;<span <p><b>Lebanon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-US-Lebanon.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/En-US-Lebanon.ogg" class="internal" title="En-US-Lebanon.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">لبنان</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Lubnān</i>, <small>Levantine Arabic pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[lɪbˈnɛːn]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Liban</i>), officially known as the <b>Lebanese Republic</b><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;nb 3&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجمهورية اللبنانية</span>&#8206;, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&#160;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Jumhūrīyah al-Lubnānīyah</i>, <small>Levantine Arabic pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[elˈʒʊmhuːɾɪjje lˈlɪbnɛːnɪjje]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République libanaise</i>), is an <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> to the north and east and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> to the south, while <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> is west across the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>. Lebanon's location at the crossroads of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabian</a> <a href="/wiki/Hinterland" title="Hinterland">hinterland</a> facilitated <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lebanon" title="History of Lebanon">its rich history</a> and shaped <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Lebanon" title="Culture of Lebanon">a cultural identity</a> of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon#Religious_groups" title="Demographics of Lebanon">religious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon" title="Demographics of Lebanon">ethnic</a> diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> At just 10,452&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,036 sq. mi.), it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">smallest recognized sovereign state</a> on the mainland <a href="/wiki/Asian_continent" class="mw-redirect" title="Asian continent">Asian continent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;nb 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_record" title="Archaeological record">evidence</a> of civilization in Lebanon dates back more than seven thousand years, predating <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-byblos_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byblos-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon was the home of the <a href="/wiki/Canaanites" class="mw-redirect" title="Canaanites">Canaanites</a>/<a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> and their kingdoms, a maritime culture that flourished for over a thousand years (<a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">c.</a> 1550–539 BC). In 64 BC, the region came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>, and eventually became one of the Empire's leading centers of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon" title="Mount Lebanon">Mount Lebanon</a> range a monastic tradition known as the <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Church" title="Maronite Church">Maronite Church</a> was established. As the <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">conquered</a> the region, the <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronites</a> held onto their religion and <a href="/wiki/Religious_identity" title="Religious identity">identity</a>. However, a new religious group, the <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a>, established themselves in Mount Lebanon as well, generating a religious divide that has lasted for centuries. During the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a>, the Maronites re-established contact with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic Church</a> and asserted their communion with Rome. The ties they established with the Latins have influenced the region into the modern era.
</p><p>The region eventually was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> from 1516 to 1918. Following the collapse of the empire after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the five provinces that constitute modern Lebanon came under the <a href="/wiki/French_Mandate_of_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="French Mandate of Lebanon">French Mandate of Lebanon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> expanded the borders of the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon_Governorate" title="Mount Lebanon Governorate">Mount Lebanon Governorate</a>, which was mostly populated by Maronites and Druze, to include more Muslims. Lebanon gained independence in 1943, establishing <a href="/wiki/Confessionalism_(politics)" title="Confessionalism (politics)">confessionalism</a>, a unique, <a href="/wiki/Consociationalism" title="Consociationalism">Consociationalism</a>-type of political system with a power-sharing mechanism based on religious communities. <a href="/wiki/Bechara_El_Khoury" title="Bechara El Khoury">Bechara El Khoury</a>, President of Lebanon during the independence, <a href="/wiki/Riad_El-Solh" class="mw-redirect" title="Riad El-Solh">Riad El-Solh</a>, first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Lebanon">Lebanese prime minister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emir_Majid_Arslan_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Emir Majid Arslan II">Emir Majid Arslan II</a>, first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Prime Ministers of Lebanon">Lebanese minister of defence</a>, are considered the founders of the modern Republic of Lebanon and are national heroes for having led the country's independence. Foreign troops withdrew completely from Lebanon on 31 December 1946,<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2011-12-01_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2011-12-01-20">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> although the country was subjected to military occupations by <a href="/wiki/Syrian_occupation_of_Lebanon" title="Syrian occupation of Lebanon">Syria</a> that lasted nearly thirty years before being withdrawn in April 2005 as well as <a href="/wiki/Israeli_occupation_of_Southern_Lebanon" title="Israeli occupation of Southern Lebanon">Israel</a> for fifteen years before being withdrawn in May 2000.
</p><p>Despite its small size,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> the country has developed a well-known <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Lebanon" title="Culture of Lebanon">culture</a> and has been highly influential in the Arab world, powered by its large <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">diaspora</a>. Before the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a> (1975–1990), the country experienced a period of relative calm and renowned prosperity, driven by tourism, agriculture, commerce, and banking.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Because of its financial power and diversity in its heyday, Lebanon was referred to as the "Switzerland of the East" during the 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and its capital, <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, attracted so many tourists that it was known as "the <a href="/wiki/Paris_of_the_East_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris of the East (disambiguation)">Paris of the Middle East</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-24">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the war, there were extensive efforts to revive the economy and rebuild national infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-25">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In spite of these troubles, Lebanon has the 7th highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index#Arab_League" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Middle_East#Statistics" title="Economy of the Middle East">GDP per capita</a> in the Arab world after the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">oil-rich economies of the Persian Gulf</a>. Lebanon has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since its founding in 1945 as well as of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> (1945), the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> (1961), <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_the_Islamic_Cooperation" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of the Islamic Cooperation</a> (1969) and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_francophonie" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation internationale de la francophonie">Organisation internationale de la francophonie</a> (1973).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon" title="Mount Lebanon">Mount Lebanon</a> originates from the <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician</a> root <i><i lang="sem" title="Semitic languages collective text">lbn</i></i> (<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%A4%8B%F0%90%A4%81%F0%90%A4%8D" class="extiw" title="wikt:𐤋𐤁𐤍">𐤋𐤁𐤍</a>) meaning "white", apparently from its snow-capped peaks.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Occurrences of the name have been found in different <a href="/wiki/Middle_Bronze_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Bronze Age">Middle Bronze Age</a> texts from the library of <a href="/wiki/Ebla" title="Ebla">Ebla</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and three of the twelve tablets of the <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">Epic of Gilgamesh</a>.
The name is recorded in <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_language" title="Egyptian language">Ancient Egyptian</a> as <i>Rmnn</i> (𓂋𓏠𓈖𓈖𓈉), where <i>R</i> stood for <a href="/wiki/Canaanite_languages" title="Canaanite languages">Canaanite</a> <i>L</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
The name occurs nearly 70 times in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_Bible" title="Hebrew Bible">Hebrew Bible</a>, as <span lang="he" dir="rtl" title="Hebrew language text">לְבָנוֹן</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Lebanon</i> as the name of an administrative unit (as opposed to the mountain range) was introduced with the <a href="/wiki/Tanzimat" title="Tanzimat">Ottoman reforms</a> of 1861, as the <i><a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon_Mutasarrifate" title="Mount Lebanon Mutasarrifate">Mount Lebanon Mutasarrifate</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">متصرفية جبل لبنان</span>&#8206;; <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <i lang="tr">Cebel-i Lübnan Mutasarrıflığı</i>), continued in the name of the <i><a href="/wiki/Greater_Lebanon" title="Greater Lebanon">State of Greater Lebanon</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">دولة لبنان الكبير</span>&#8206; <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Dawlat Lubnān al-Kabīr</i></i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">État du Grand Liban</i>) in 1920, and eventually in the name of the sovereign <i>Republic of Lebanon</i>  (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجمهورية اللبنانية</span>&#8206; <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization"><i>al-Jumhūrīyah al-Lubnānīyah</i></i>) upon its independence in 1943.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Lebanon%22">"Lebanon"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Lebanon%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Lebanon%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Lebanon%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Lebanon%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Lebanon%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lebanon" title="History of Lebanon">History of Lebanon</a></div>
<p>The borders of contemporary Lebanon are a product of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a> of 1920.
Its territory was the core of the Bronze Age <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> (<a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a>) city-states. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>, it was part of numerous succeeding empires throughout ancient history, including the  <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian Empire">Egyptian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia_under_Assyrian_rule" title="Phoenicia under Assyrian rule">Assyrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia_under_Babylonian_rule" title="Phoenicia under Babylonian rule">Babylonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Phoenicia" class="mw-redirect" title="Achaemenid Phoenicia">Achaemenid Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia_under_Hellenistic_rule" title="Phoenicia under Hellenistic rule">Hellenistic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia_under_Roman_rule" title="Phoenicia under Roman rule">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanid Persian</a> empires.
</p><p>After the 7th-century <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant" title="Muslim conquest of the Levant">Muslim conquest of the Levant</a>, it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Rashidun_Caliphate" title="Rashidun Caliphate">Rashidun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid</a> <a href="/wiki/Great_Seljuq_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Seljuq Empire">Seljuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid</a> empires.
The <a href="/wiki/Crusader_state" class="mw-redirect" title="Crusader state">crusader state</a> of the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tripoli" title="County of Tripoli">County of Tripoli</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Raymond_IV_of_Toulouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Raymond IV of Toulouse">Raymond IV of Toulouse</a> in 1102, encompassed most of present-day Lebanon, falling to the <a href="/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo)" title="Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)">Mamluk Sultanate</a> in 1289 and finally to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1517. With the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">dissolution of the Ottoman Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Lebanon" title="Greater Lebanon">Greater Lebanon</a> fell under <a href="/wiki/French_Mandate_for_Syria_and_the_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="French Mandate for Syria and the Lebanon">French mandate</a> in 1920, and gained independence under president <a href="/wiki/Bechara_El_Khoury" title="Bechara El Khoury">Bechara El Khoury</a> in 1943.
Lebanon's history since independence has been marked by alternating periods of political stability and prosperity based on <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>'s position as a regional center for finance and trade, interspersed with political turmoil and armed conflict  (<a href="/wiki/1948_Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_War" title="1948 Arab–Israeli War">1948 Arab–Israeli War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Civil_War" title="Lebanese Civil War">Lebanese Civil War</a> 1975–1990, 2005 <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Revolution" title="Cedar Revolution">Cedar Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Lebanon_conflict" title="2007 Lebanon conflict">2007 Lebanon conflict</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9308_Lebanese_protests" title="2006–08 Lebanese protests">2006–08 Lebanese protests</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_conflict_in_Lebanon" title="2008 conflict in Lebanon">2008 conflict in Lebanon</a>, and since 2011 <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War_spillover_in_Lebanon" title="Syrian Civil War spillover in Lebanon">Syrian Civil War spillover</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Lebanon">Ancient Lebanon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient Lebanon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_ancient_Lebanon" title="History of ancient Lebanon">History of ancient Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PhoenicianTrade.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/PhoenicianTrade.png/220px-PhoenicianTrade.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/PhoenicianTrade.png/330px-PhoenicianTrade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/PhoenicianTrade.png/440px-PhoenicianTrade.png 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="418" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PhoenicianTrade.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Phoenicia and trade routes</div></div></div>
<p>Evidence dating back to an early settlement in Lebanon was found in <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">Byblos</a>, considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Oldest_continuously_inhabited_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Oldest continuously inhabited cities">oldest continuously inhabited cities</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-byblos_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-byblos-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The evidence dates back to earlier than 5000 BC. Archaeologists discovered remnants of prehistoric huts with crushed limestone floors, primitive weapons, and burial jars left by the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copper_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Copper Age">Chalcolithic</a> fishing communities who lived on the shore of the Mediterranean Sea over 7,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanon was a part of northern <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaan</a>, and consequently became the homeland of Canaanite descendants – the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, a seafaring people who spread across the Mediterranean in the first millennium BC .<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The most prominent Phoenician cities were <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">Byblos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sidon" title="Sidon">Sidon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tyre,_Lebanon" title="Tyre, Lebanon">Tyre</a>, while their most famous colonies were <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> in present-day  <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Canaanite_languages" title="Canaanite languages">Canaanite-Phoenicians</a> are credited with the invention of the <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_alphabet" title="Phoenician alphabet">Phoenician alphabet</a>. The cities of Phoenicia were incorporated into the Persian <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> by <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">Cyrus the Great</a> in 539 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The Phoenician city-states were later incorporated into the empire of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tyre_(332_BC)" title="Siege of Tyre (332 BC)">Siege of Tyre</a> in 332 BC.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Maronites.2C_Druze.2C_and_the_Crusades"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Maronites,_Druze,_and_the_Crusades">Maronites, Druze, and the Crusades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Maronites, Druze, and the Crusades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_(1289).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg/220px-Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="349" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg/330px-Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg/440px-Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_%281289%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1720" data-file-height="2725" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_Tripoli_Painting_(1289).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Tripoli_(1289)" title="Fall of Tripoli (1289)">Fall of Tripoli</a> to the Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Mamluk" title="Mamluk">Mamluks</a> and destruction of the Crusader state, the County of Tripoli, 1289</div></div></div>
<p>The region that is now Lebanon, as with the rest of Syria and much of <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>, became a major center of Christianity in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> during the early spread of the religion. During the late 4th and early 5th century, a hermit named <a href="/wiki/Maron" title="Maron">Maron</a> established a monastic tradition focused on the importance of <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asceticism" title="Asceticism">asceticism</a>, near the Mediterranean mountain range known as <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon" title="Mount Lebanon">Mount Lebanon</a>. The monks who followed Maron spread his teachings among Lebanese in the region. These Christians came to be known as <a href="/wiki/Maronite" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite">Maronites</a> and moved into the mountains to avoid religious persecution by Roman authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the frequent <a href="/wiki/Roman-Persian_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman-Persian Wars">Roman-Persian Wars</a> that lasted for many centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Sassanid_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassanid Empire">Sassanid Persians</a> occupied what is now Lebanon from 619 till 629.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the 7th century the Muslim Arabs <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Syria" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim conquest of Syria">conquered Syria</a> establishing a new regime to replace the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>. Though Islam and the Arabic language were officially dominant under this new regime, the general populace nonetheless only gradually converted from Christianity and the Syriac language. The Maronite community in particular managed to maintain a large degree of autonomy despite the succession of rulers over Lebanon and Syria.
</p><p>During the 11th century the <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a> faith emerged from a branch of <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a>. The new faith gained followers in the southern portion of Mount Lebanon. The northern portion of Mount Lebanon was ruled by Druze feudal families to the early 14th century which was then brought to an end by the Mamluk invasion. The Maronite population increased gradually in Northern Mount Lebanon and the Druze have remained in Southern Mount Lebanon until the modern era. In the south of Lebanon, <a href="/wiki/Jabal_Amel" title="Jabal Amel">Jabal Amel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baalbek" title="Baalbek">Baalbek</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Beqaa_Valley" title="Beqaa Valley">Beqaa Valley</a> was ruled by Shia feudal families under the Mamluks and the Ottoman Empire. Major cities on the coast, <a href="/wiki/Acre,_Israel" title="Acre, Israel">Acre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, and others, were directly administered by the Muslim Caliphs and the people became more fully absorbed by the Arab culture.
</p><p>Following the fall of Roman <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> to the Muslim Turks, the Byzantines put out a call to the Pope in Rome for assistance in the 11th century. The result was a series of wars known as the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> launched by the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish Empire">Franks</a> in Western Europe to reclaim the former Byzantine Christian territories in the Eastern Mediterranean, especially <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a> (the <i><a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a></i>). The <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">First Crusade</a> succeeded in temporarily establishing the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Jerusalem" title="Kingdom of Jerusalem">Kingdom of Jerusalem</a> and the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Tripoli" title="County of Tripoli">County of Tripoli</a> as Roman Catholic Christian states along the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> These crusader states made a lasting impact on the region, though their control was limited, and the region returned to full Muslim control after two centuries following the conquest by the Mamluks.
</p><p>One of the most lasting effects of the Crusades in this region was the contact between the Franks (i.e. the French) and the Maronites. Unlike most other Christian communities in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a>, who swore allegiance to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> or other local patriarchs, the Maronites proclaimed allegiance to the Pope in Rome. As such the Franks saw them as Roman Catholic brethren. These initial contacts led to centuries of support for the Maronites from France and Italy, even after the fall of the Crusader states in the region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_Lebanon_and_French_Mandate">Ottoman Lebanon and French Mandate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ottoman Lebanon and French Mandate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Mount_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Emirate of Mount Lebanon">Emirate of Mount Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sidon_Eyalet" title="Sidon Eyalet">Sidon Eyalet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mount_Lebanon_Mutasarrifate" title="Mount Lebanon Mutasarrifate">Mount Lebanon Mutasarrifate</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg/220px-DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg/330px-DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg/440px-DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DeirAlQamar-FakhredinePalace.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fakhreddine_II_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Fakhreddine II Palace">Fakhreddine II Palace</a>, 17th century</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_as_envisaged_by_French_General_Charles-Marie-Napol%C3%A9on_de_Beaufort_d%27Hautpoul_Beaufort_d%27Hautpoul_in_1862.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
