<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Lebanon" title="Economy of Lebanon">Economy of Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg/220px-Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg/330px-Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg/440px-Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2668" data-file-height="2085" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Lebanon 's product exports in 28 color-coded categories.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/en:Constitution_of_Lebanon#preamble_f" class="extiw" title="wikisource:en:Constitution of Lebanon">Lebanon's constitution</a> states that 'the economic system is free and ensures private initiative and the right to private property'. Lebanon's economy follows a <a href="/wiki/Laissez-faire" title="Laissez-faire">laissez-faire</a> model.<sup id="cite_ref-expus_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expus-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Most of the economy is <a href="/wiki/Dollarized" class="mw-redirect" title="Dollarized">dollarized</a>, and the country has no restrictions on the movement of capital across its borders.<sup id="cite_ref-expus_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expus-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The Lebanese government's intervention in foreign trade is minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-expus_157-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expus-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Lebanese economy went through a significant expansion after the <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_war_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanon war 2006">war of 2006</a>, with growth averaging 9.1% between 2007 and 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_growth_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank_growth-158">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> After 2011 the local economy was affected by the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian civil war</a>, growing by a yearly average of 1.7% on the 2011-2016 period and by 1.5% in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_growth_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank_growth-158">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the size of the GDP was estimated to be $54.1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Fact_Book_-_Lebanon_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Fact_Book_-_Lebanon-159">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanon has a very high level of public debt and large external financing needs.<sup id="cite_ref-expus_157-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expus-157">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> The 2010 public debt exceeded 150.7% of GDP, ranking fourth highest in the world as a percentage of GDP, though down from 154.8% in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> At the end 2008, finance minister <a href="/wiki/Mohamad_Chatah" title="Mohamad Chatah">Mohamad Chatah</a> stated that the debt was going to reach $47&#160;billion in that year and would increase to $49&#160;billion if privatization of two telecoms companies did not occur.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Daily_Star_(Lebanon)" class="mw-redirect" title="Daily Star (Lebanon)">Daily Star</a> wrote that exorbitant debt levels have "slowed down the economy and reduced the government's spending on essential development projects".<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The urban population in Lebanon is noted for its commercial enterprise.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Emigration has yielded Lebanese "commercial networks" throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Remittances from Lebanese abroad total $8.2&#160;billion<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> and account for one fifth of the country's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon has the largest proportion of skilled labor among Arab States.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Investment_Development_Authority_of_Lebanon" title="Investment Development Authority of Lebanon">Investment Development Authority of Lebanon</a> was established with the aim of promoting investment in Lebanon. In 2001, Investment Law No.360<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> was enacted to reinforce the organisation's mission.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Lebanon" title="Agriculture in Lebanon">agricultural sector</a> employs 12% of the total <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">workforce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-168">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Agriculture contributed to 5.9% of the country's GDP in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon's proportion of cultivable land is the highest in the Arab world,<sup id="cite_ref-agriculture_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-agriculture-170">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Major produce includes apples, peaches, oranges, and lemons.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Commodity_market" title="Commodity market">commodities market</a> in Lebanon includes substantial <a href="/wiki/Gold_coin" title="Gold coin">gold coin</a> production, however according to <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">International Air Transport Association</a> <b>(IATA)</b> standards, they must be declared upon exportation to any foreign country.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil</a> has recently been discovered inland and in the seabed between Lebanon, Cyprus, Israel and Egypt and talks are underway between <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> to reach an agreement regarding the exploration of these resources. The seabed separating Lebanon and Cyprus is believed to hold significant quantities of crude oil and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Industry in Lebanon is mainly limited to small businesses that reassemble and package imported parts. In 2004, industry ranked second in workforce, with 26% of the Lebanese working population,<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_168-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-168">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> and second in GDP contribution, with 21% of Lebanon's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nearly 65% of the Lebanese workforce attain employment in the services sector.<sup id="cite_ref-workforce_168-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-workforce-168">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> The GDP contribution, accordingly, amounts to roughly 67.3% of the annual Lebanese GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> However, dependence on the tourism and banking sectors leaves the economy vulnerable to political instability.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-25">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanese banks are high on liquidity and reputed for their security.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_Banks_immune_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon_Banks_immune-173">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon was one of the only seven countries in the world in which the value of the stock markets increased in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_2008_profit_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon_2008_profit-174">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 10 May 2013 the Lebanese minister of energy and water clarified that seismic images of the Lebanese's sea bed are undergoing detailed explanation of their contents and that up till now, approximately 10% have been covered. Preliminary inspection of the results showed, with more than 50% probability, that 10% of Lebanon's exclusive economic zone contained up to 660 million barrels of oil and up to 30×10<sup>12</sup> cu ft of gas.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Syrian crisis has significantly affected Lebanese economic and financial situation. The demographic pressure imposed by the Syrian refugees now living in Lebanon has led to competition in the labour market. As a direct consequence unemployment has doubled in three years, reaching 20% in 2014. A loss of 14% of wages regarding the salary of less-skilled workers has also been registered. The financial constraints were also felt: the poverty rate increased with 170.000 Lebanese falling under the poverty threshold. In the period between 2012 and 2014, the public spending increased by $1 billion and losses amounted to $7.5 billion. Expenditures related only to the Syrian refugees were estimated by the Central Bank of Lebanon as $4.5 billion every year.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle.fanack.com_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle.fanack.com-176">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/220px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/330px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG/440px-Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="609" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanese_real_GDP_Growth_in_%25.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lebanese real GDP growth</div></div></div>
<p>In the 1950s, GDP growth was the second highest in the world. Despite not having oil reserves, Lebanon, as the banking center of the Middle East and one of the trading centers, had a high national income.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 1975–1990 civil war heavily damaged Lebanon's economic infrastructure,<sup id="cite_ref-Stinson_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stinson-144">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> cut national output by half, and all but ended Lebanon's position as a West Asian <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">entrepôt</a> and banking hub.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The subsequent period of relative peace enabled the central government to restore control in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, begin collecting taxes, and regain access to key port and government facilities. Economic recovery has been helped by a financially sound banking system and resilient small- and medium-scale manufacturers, with family remittances, banking services, manufactured and farm exports, and international aid as the main sources of foreign exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-cia2001_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia2001-178">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Until July 2006, Lebanon enjoyed considerable stability, Beirut's reconstruction was almost complete,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> and increasing numbers of tourists poured into the nation's resorts.<sup id="cite_ref-tourism_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tourism-24">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The economy witnessed growth, with bank assets reaching over 75&#160;billion US dollars,<sup id="cite_ref-economy-stat_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-stat-180">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">Market capitalization</a> was also at an all-time high, estimated at $10.9&#160;billion at the end of the second quarter of 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-economy-stat_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economy-stat-180">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The month-long <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 war</a> severely damaged Lebanon's fragile economy, especially the tourism sector. According to a preliminary report published by the Lebanese <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Finance (Lebanon)">Ministry of Finance</a> on 30 August 2006, a major economic decline was expected as a result of the fighting.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the course of 2008 Lebanon rebuilt its infrastructure mainly in the real estate and tourism sectors, resulting in a comparatively robust post war economy. Major contributors to the reconstruction of Lebanon include <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> (with US$1.5&#160;billion pledged),<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> the European Union (with about $1&#160;billion)<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> and a few other Persian Gulf countries with contributions of up to $800&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Lebanon" title="Tourism in Lebanon">Tourism in Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg/170px-Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg/255px-Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg/340px-Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2824" data-file-height="4237" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek_-_temple_of_Jupiter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Baalbek" title="Baalbek">Baalbek</a>, temple of <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_(mythology)" title="Jupiter (mythology)">Jupiter</a></div></div></div>
<p>The tourism industry accounts for about 10% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-lebtourecon_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebtourecon-185">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon managed to attract around 1,333,000 tourists in 2008, thus placing it as rank 79 out of 191 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, <i>The New York Times</i> ranked Beirut the No.&#160;1 travel destination worldwide due to its nightlife and hospitality.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In January 2010, the Ministry of Tourism announced that 1,851,081 tourists had visited Lebanon in 2009, a 39% increase from 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-lebanon-tourism1_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebanon-tourism1-188">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Lebanon hosted the largest number of tourists to date, eclipsing the previous record set before the Lebanese Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_2009_Tourism_Record_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_2009_Tourism_Record-189">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Tourist arrivals reached two million in 2010, but fell by 37% for the first 10 months of 2012, a decline caused by the war in neighbouring Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-lebtourecon_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lebtourecon-185">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anjar-109900.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/220px-Anjar-109900.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/330px-Anjar-109900.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Anjar-109900.jpg/440px-Anjar-109900.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anjar-109900.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arches at the ruins of Anjar</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, Jordan, and Japan are the three most popular origin countries of foreign tourists to Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The recent influx of Japanese tourists has caused the recent rise in popularity of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_Cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese Cuisine">Japanese Cuisine</a> in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Lebanon" title="Demographics of Lebanon">Demographics of Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese people</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tripoli,_Lebanon_(5074428682).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg/170px-Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg/255px-Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg/340px-Tripoli%2C_Lebanon_%285074428682%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tripoli,_Lebanon_(5074428682).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artisan in Tripoli</div></div></div>
<p>The population of Lebanon was estimated to be 6,006,668 in 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> however, no official census has been conducted since 1932 due to the sensitive <a href="/wiki/Confessionalism_(politics)" title="Confessionalism (politics)">confessional political balance</a> between Lebanon's various religious groups.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Identifying all Lebanese as ethnically <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arab</a> is a widely employed example of <a href="/wiki/Panethnicity" title="Panethnicity">panethnicity</a> since in reality, the Lebanese "are descended from many different peoples who are either indigenous, or have occupied, invaded, or settled this corner of the world", making Lebanon, "a mosaic of closely interrelated cultures".<sup id="cite_ref-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406-193">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> While at first glance, this ethnic, linguistic, religious and denominational diversity might seem to cause civil and political unrest, "for much of Lebanon’s history this multitudinous diversity of religious communities has coexisted with little conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stokes,_Jamie_page_406-193">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> fell from 5.00 in 1971 to 1.75 in 2004. Fertility rates vary considerably among the different religious groups: in 2004, it was 2.10 for <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shiites</a>, 1.76 <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunnis</a> and 1.61 for <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanon has witnessed a series of migration waves: over 1,800,000 people emigrated from the country in the 1975–2011 period.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Millions of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_diaspora" title="Lebanese diaspora">people of Lebanese descent</a> are spread throughout the world, mostly Christians,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> especially in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> has the largest expatriate population.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> <i>(See <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Brazilian">Lebanese Brazilians</a>)</i>. Large numbers of Lebanese migrated to <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> particularly to the <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> (home to over 100,000 Lebanese)<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> (roughly 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people_in_Senegal" title="Lebanese people in Senegal">Lebanese</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> is home to over 270,000 <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Australian">Lebanese</a> (1999 est.).<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, there is also a large Lebanese diaspora of approximately 250,000–700,000 people having Lebanese descent. (see <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Canadians" title="Lebanese Canadians">Lebanese Canadians</a>). Another region with a significant diaspora is the Persian Gulf, where the countries of Bahrain, Kuwait, Oman, Qatar (around 25,000 people),<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Saudi Arabia and UAE act as host countries to many Lebanese.
</p><p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Lebanon was host to over 1,600,000 <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum</a> seekers: 449,957 from <a href="/wiki/Palestinians_in_Lebanon" title="Palestinians in Lebanon">Palestine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> 3,515 from <a href="/wiki/Iraqis_in_Lebanon" title="Iraqis in Lebanon">Iraq</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> over 1,100,000 from <a href="/wiki/Syrians_in_Lebanon" title="Syrians in Lebanon">Syria</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> and 4,000 from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>.  According to the Economic and Social Commission for Western Asia of the United Nations, among the Syrian refugees, 71% live in poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-chronicle.fanack.com_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chronicle.fanack.com-176">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The latest estimates by the United Nations put the number of <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugees of the Syrian civil war">Syrian refugees</a> at more than 1,250,000.<sup id="cite_ref-refugees_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-refugees-92">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the last three decades, lengthy and destructive <a href="/wiki/Armed_conflict" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed conflict">armed conflicts</a> have ravaged the country. The majority of Lebanese have been affected by armed conflict; those with direct personal experience include 75% of the population, and most others report suffering a range of hardships. In total, almost the entire population (96%) has been affected in
some way – either personally or because of the wider consequences of armed conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>

<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Baalbek" title="Baalbek">Baalbek</a></td>
<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Beqaa_Governorate" title="Beqaa Governorate">Bekaa</a></td>
