<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Lebanon" title="Religion in Lebanon">Religion in Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Islam in Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christianity in Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secularism_in_Lebanon" title="Secularism in Lebanon">Secularism in Lebanon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Lebanon" title="Irreligion in Lebanon">Irreligion in Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:SaddleBrown"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 272.37868371332px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:24.868988716485px 96.858316112863px 0 0; border-top-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Lebanon (est. 2014)
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Islam</a> (54%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christianity</a> (40.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SaddleBrown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a> (5.6%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/120px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/180px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg/240px-Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="3484" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lebanon_religious_groups_distribution.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of main religious groups of Lebanon according to last municipal election data.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Lebanon is the most religiously diverse country in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> estimates the following: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a> 54% (27% <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni Islam</a>, 27% <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shia Islam</a>), <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a> 40.5% (includes 21% <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite</a> Catholic, 8% <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a> Catholic, 1% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestant</a>, 5.5% other Christian), <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a> 5.6%, very small numbers of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Jews">Jews</a>, Baha'is, <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> A study conducted by the Lebanese Information Center and based on voter registration numbers shows that by 2011 the Christian population was stable compared to that of previous years, making up 34.35% of the population; Muslims, the Druze included, were 65.47% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/World_Values_Survey" title="World Values Survey">World Values Survey</a> of 2014 put the percentage of <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheists</a> in Lebanon at 3.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-WVS_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WVS-210">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is believed that there has been a decline in the ratio of Christians to Muslims over the past 60 years, due to higher emigration rates of Christians, and a higher birth rate in the Muslim population.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> When the last census was held in 1932, Christians made up 53% of Lebanon's population.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_194-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In 1956, it was estimated that the population was 54% Christian and 44% Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-demo-reality_194-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demo-reality-194">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A demographic study conducted by the research firm <a href="/w/index.php?title=Statistics_Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Statistics Lebanon (page does not exist)">Statistics Lebanon</a> found that approximately 27% of the population was <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni</a>, 27% <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shia</a>, 21% <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite</a>, 8% <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a>, 5% <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a>, and 1% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestant</a>, with the remaining 6% mostly belonging to smaller non-native to Lebanon Christian denominations.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_211-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other sources like <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid-based</a> diary <i><a href="/wiki/La_Raz%C3%B3n_(Madrid)" title="La Razón (Madrid)">La Razón</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> estimate the percentage of Christians to be around 53%.
</p><p>Because the relative size of confessional groups remains a sensitive issue, a national census has not been conducted since 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_211-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> There are 18 state-recognized religious sects – four <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a>, 12 <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Druze_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Druze in Lebanon">Druze</a>, and one <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Jews">Jewish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedom_211-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedom-211">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Islam in Lebanon">Sunni residents</a> primarily live in Tripoli, Western Beirut, the Southern coast of Lebanon, and Northern Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Islam in Lebanon">Shi'a residents</a> primarily live in Southern Beirut, the <a href="/wiki/Beqaa_Valley" title="Beqaa Valley">Beqaa Valley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Lebanon" title="Southern Lebanon">Southern Lebanon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_214-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Maronite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Maronite Christianity in Lebanon">Maronite residents</a> primarily live in Eastern Beirut and the mountains of Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_214-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> They are the largest Christian community in Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_glossary_214-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC_glossary-214">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a>, the second largest Christian community in Lebanon, primarily live in Koura, Beirut, Rachaya, Matn, Aley, Akkar, in the countryside around Tripoli, Hasbaya and Marjeyoun. They are a minority of 10% in Zahle.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Greek Catholics live mainly in Beirut, on the eastern slopes of the Lebanon mountains and in Zahle which is predominantly Greek Catholic.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the Christian village of Hadat, there have been a municipal ban on Muslims from buying or renting property. It has been claimed that it is due to the underlying fear of mixing with one another's salvation since for three decades, the village of Hadat has been primarily Christian.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">French language in Lebanon</a></div>
<p>Article 11 of Lebanon's Constitution states that "Arabic is the official national language. A law determines the cases in which the <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French language</a> is to be used".<sup id="cite_ref-article_11_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-article_11-217">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The majority of Lebanese people speak <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a>, which is grouped in a larger category called <a href="/wiki/Levantine_Arabic" title="Levantine Arabic">Levantine Arabic</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> is mostly used in magazines, newspapers, and formal broadcast media. <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Sign_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Sign Language">Lebanese Sign Language</a> is the language of the deaf community. Almost 40% of Lebanese are considered <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">francophone</a>, and another 15% "partial francophone", and 70% of Lebanon's secondary schools use French as a second language of instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-NadeauBarlow2008_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NadeauBarlow2008-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> By comparison, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is used as a secondary language in 30% of Lebanon's secondary schools.<sup id="cite_ref-NadeauBarlow2008_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NadeauBarlow2008-218">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The use of French is a legacy of France's historic ties to the region, including its <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">League of Nations mandate</a> over Lebanon following World War I; as of 2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, some 20% of the population used French on a daily basis.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-219">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The use of Arabic by Lebanon's educated youth is declining, as they usually prefer to speak in French and, to a lesser extent, English, which are seen as more fashionable.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>English is increasingly used in science and business interactions.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_nationality_law" title="Lebanese nationality law">Lebanese citizens</a> of <a href="/wiki/Armenians_in_Lebanon" title="Armenians in Lebanon">Armenian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks_in_Lebanon" title="Greeks in Lebanon">Greek</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Assyrians_in_Lebanon" title="Assyrians in Lebanon">Assyrian</a> descent often speak their ancestral languages with varying degrees of fluency. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were around 150,000 Armenians in Lebanon, or around 5% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Lebanon" title="Culture of Lebanon">Culture of Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/220px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/330px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg/440px-Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baalbek-Bacchus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Bacchus" title="Temple of Bacchus">Temple of Bacchus</a> is considered one of the best preserved <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> temples in the world, c. 150 AD</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Byblos-109933.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Byblos-109933.jpg/220px-Byblos-109933.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Byblos-109933.jpg/330px-Byblos-109933.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Byblos-109933.jpg/440px-Byblos-109933.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Byblos-109933.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ruins at port of <a href="/wiki/Byblos" title="Byblos">Byblos</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The culture of Lebanon reflects the legacy of various civilizations spanning thousands of years. Originally home to the <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a><a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">- Phoenicians</a>, and then subsequently conquered and occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Assyria" title="Assyria">Assyrians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Persia">Persians</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, the Arabs, the <a href="/wiki/Fatimids" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a>, the Crusaders, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a> and most recently the French, Lebanese culture has over the millennia evolved by borrowing from all of these groups. Lebanon's diverse population, composed of different ethnic and religious groups, has further contributed to the country's festivals, musical styles and literature as well as cuisine. Despite the ethnic, linguistic, religious and denominational diversity of the Lebanese, they "share an almost common culture".<sup id="cite_ref-StokesJamie_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StokesJamie-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a> is universally spoken while food, music, and literature are deep-rooted "in wider Mediterranean and Arab Levantine norms".<sup id="cite_ref-StokesJamie_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StokesJamie-225">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Beige marble statue of a stout young child aged about two years old lying on his left side. The child&#39;s head is shaved, his eyes gaze over the viewer&#39;s shoulder and his lower body is covered in a draping cloth that hangs limply between his flexed feet. The child supports his torso with his left hand in which he holds an unidentifiable object, he also holds a small bird in his right hand. The sculpture rests on a heavy socle inscribed with barely visible letters spanning the upper part of the socle vertically." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/220px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/330px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg/440px-Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2378" data-file-height="1788" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Votive_statue_from_eshmun.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Votive marble statue of a royal child, inscribed in Phoenician from the <a href="/wiki/Eshmun" title="Eshmun">Eshmun</a> sanctuary, c. 400s BC</div></div></div>
<p>In visual arts, <a href="/wiki/Moustafa_Farroukh" title="Moustafa Farroukh">Moustafa Farroukh</a> was one of Lebanon's most prominent painters of the 20th century. Formally trained in Rome and Paris, he exhibited in venues from Paris to New York to Beirut over his career.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> Many more contemporary artists are currently active, such as <a href="/wiki/Walid_Raad" title="Walid Raad">Walid Raad</a>, a contemporary media artist currently residing in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the field of photography, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Image_Foundation" title="Arab Image Foundation">Arab Image Foundation</a> has a collection of over 400,000 photographs from Lebanon and the Middle East. The photographs can be viewed in a research center and various events and publications have been produced in Lebanon and worldwide to promote the collection.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In literature, <a href="/wiki/Khalil_Gibran" title="Khalil Gibran">Khalil Gibran</a> is the third best-selling poet of all time, behind <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laozi" title="Laozi">Laozi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> He is particularly known for his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prophet_(book)" title="The Prophet (book)">The Prophet</a></i> (1923), which has been translated into more than twenty different languages and is the second best selling book in the 20th century behind <a href="/wiki/The_Bible" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bible">the Bible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ameen_Rihani" title="Ameen Rihani">Ameen Rihani</a> was a major figure in the mahjar literary movement developed by Arab emigrants in North America, and an early theorist of <a href="/wiki/Arab_nationalism" title="Arab nationalism">Arab nationalism</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mikha%27il_Na%27ima" title="Mikha&#39;il Na&#39;ima">Mikha'il Na'ima</a> is widely recognized as one of the most important figures in modern Arabic letters and one of the most important spiritual writers of the 20th century.
</p><p>Several contemporary Lebanese writers have also achieved international success; including <a href="/wiki/Elias_Khoury" title="Elias Khoury">Elias Khoury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amin_Maalouf" title="Amin Maalouf">Amin Maalouf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hanan_al-Shaykh" title="Hanan al-Shaykh">Hanan al-Shaykh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georges_Schehad%C3%A9" title="Georges Schehadé">Georges Schehadé</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Lebanon" title="Music of Lebanon">Music of Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/180px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/270px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg/360px-Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="753" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fairuz_in_btd_concert_2001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fairuz" title="Fairuz">Fairuz</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg/180px-Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg/270px-Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg/360px-Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casino_du_Liban_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lydia_Canaan" title="Lydia Canaan">Lydia Canaan</a>, first rock star in the Middle East</div></div></div>
<p>While traditional folk music remains popular in Lebanon, modern music reconciling Western and traditional Arabic styles, pop, and <a href="/wiki/Fusion_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fusion (music)">fusion</a> are rapidly advancing in popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-Traditional_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Traditional-230">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Lebanese artists like <a href="/wiki/Fairuz" title="Fairuz">Fairuz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wadih_El_Safi" title="Wadih El Safi">Wadih El Safi</a> or Sabah are widely known and appreciated in Lebanon and in the Arab world. Lebanese singer <a href="/wiki/Lydia_Canaan" title="Lydia Canaan">Lydia Canaan</a> is listed in the catalog of the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame and Museum">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame and Museum</a>'s Library and Archives in Cleveland, Ohio, USA<sup id="cite_ref-rock_hall_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rock_hall-231">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Star_Rock_Hall_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Star_Rock_Hall-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> as the first rock star of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Daily_Star_Rock_Hall_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily_Star_Rock_Hall-232">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Radio stations feature a variety of music, including traditional Lebanese, classical Arabic, Armenian<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and modern French, English, American, and <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin</a> tunes.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_cinema">Media and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Media and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Lebanon" title="Cinema of Lebanon">cinema of Lebanon</a>, according to film critic and historian, Roy Armes, was the only cinema in the Arabic-speaking region, other than Egypt's, that could amount to a national cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> Cinema in Lebanon has been in existence since the 1920s, and the country has produced over 500 films.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
The <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Lebanon" title="Media of Lebanon">media of Lebanon</a> is not only a regional center of production but also the most liberal and free in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> According to Press freedom's <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>, "the media have more freedom in Lebanon than in any other Arab country".<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Despite its small population and geographic size, Lebanon plays an influential role in the production of information in the Arab world and is "at the core of a regional media network with global implications".<sup id="cite_ref-b1_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-243">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays_and_festivals">Holidays and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Holidays and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Lebanon" title="Public holidays in Lebanon">Public holidays in Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg/220px-Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg/330px-Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg/440px-Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beiteddine_Palace_InnerCourtyard.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Palace" title="Beiteddine Palace">Beiteddine Palace</a>, venue of the <a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Festival" title="Beiteddine Festival">Beiteddine Festival</a></div></div></div>
<p>Lebanon celebrates national and both <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Lebanon" title="Christianity in Lebanon">Christian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Lebanon" title="Islam in Lebanon">Muslim</a> holidays. Christian holidays are celebrated following both the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Gregorian Calendar">Gregorian Calendar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julian_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian Calendar">Julian Calendar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodox Christianity in Lebanon">Greek Orthodox</a> (with the exception of Easter), <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Lebanon">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestantism in Lebanon">Protestants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Melkite_Christianity_in_Lebanon" class="mw-redirect" title="Melkite Christianity in Lebanon">Melkite</a> Christians follow the Gregorian Calendar and thus celebrate Christmas on 25 December. Armenian <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Apostolic</a> Christians celebrate Christmas on 6 January, as they follow the Julian Calendar. Muslim holidays are followed based on the Islamic lunar calendar. Muslim holidays that are celebrated include Eid al-Fitr (the three-day feast at the end of the Ramadan month), Eid al-Adha (The Feast of the Sacrifice) which is celebrated during the annual pilgrimage to Mecca and also celebrates Abraham's willingness to sacrifice his son to God, the Birth of the Prophet Muhammad, and Ashura (the Shiite Day of Mourning). Lebanon's National Holidays include Workers Day, Independence day, and Martyrs Day.
</p><p>Music festivals, often hosted at historical sites, are a customary element of Lebanese culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Festivals_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Festivals-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Among the most famous are <a href="/wiki/Baalbeck_International_Festival" title="Baalbeck International Festival">Baalbeck International Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byblos_International_Festival" title="Byblos International Festival">Byblos International Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beiteddine_Festival" title="Beiteddine Festival">Beiteddine International Festival</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jouniehinternationalfestival.com/">Jounieh International Festival</a>, Broumana Festival, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.batrounfestival.org/">Batroun International Festival</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.facebook.com/ehmejfestival/">Ehmej Festival</a>, Dhour Chwer Festival and Tyr Festival.<sup id="cite_ref-Festivals_244-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Festivals-244">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> These festivals are promoted by Lebanon's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Tourism (Lebanon)">Ministry of Tourism</a>. Lebanon hosts about 15 concerts from international performers each year, ranking 1st for nightlife in the Middle East, and 6th worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_cuisine" title="Lebanese cuisine">Lebanese cuisine</a></div>
<p>Lebanese cuisine is similar to those of many countries in the Eastern Mediterranean, such as <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>.
</p><p>The Lebanese national dishes are the <a href="/wiki/Kibbe" class="mw-redirect" title="Kibbe">kibbe</a>, a meat pie made from finely minced <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">lamb</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burghul" class="mw-redirect" title="Burghul">burghul</a> (cracked <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Tabbouleh" title="Tabbouleh">tabbouleh</a>, a salad made from <a href="/wiki/Parsley" title="Parsley">parsley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, and burghul. The national beverage is <a href="/wiki/Arak_(drink)" title="Arak (drink)">arak</a>, a strong <a href="/wiki/Anise" title="Anise">anise</a>-flavored liquor made from fermented <a href="/wiki/Grape_juice" title="Grape juice">grape juice</a>. It is usually drunk with water and ice, which turns the clear liquid milky-white, and usually accompanies food. Arak is a strong spirit similar to the Greek ouzo and the Turkish raki.
</p><p>Lebanese restaurant meals begin with a wide array of <a href="/wiki/Mezze" class="mw-redirect" title="Mezze">mezze</a> - small savoury dishes, such as dips, salads, and pastries. The mezze are typically followed by a selection of grilled <a href="/wiki/Meat" title="Meat">meat</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a>. In general, meals are finished with <a href="/wiki/Arabic_coffee" title="Arabic coffee">Arabic coffee</a> and fresh <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>, though sometimes a selection of traditional sweets will be offered as well.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/M%27Juhdara" class="mw-redirect" title="M&#39;Juhdara">M'Juhdara</a>, a thick stew of <a href="/wiki/Onions" class="mw-redirect" title="Onions">onions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lentils" class="mw-redirect" title="Lentils">lentils</a>, is sometimes considered poor man's fare and is often eaten around <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">Lent</a> by people in the Lebanese diaspora.
</p><p>Beirut and its environs contain many restaurants of various national origins. At the same time, <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> is growing in popularity and a number of vineyards currently exist in the <a href="/wiki/Bekaa_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Bekaa valley">Bekaa valley</a> and elsewhere. <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">Beer</a> is also highly popular and Lebanon produces a number of local beers, of which <a href="/wiki/Almaza" class="mw-redirect" title="Almaza">almaza</a> is perhaps the most popular.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Lebanon" title="Sport in Lebanon">Sport in Lebanon</a></div>
<p>Lebanon has six <a href="/wiki/Skiing_in_Lebanon" title="Skiing in Lebanon">ski resorts</a>. Because of Lebanon's unique geography, it is possible to go skiing in the morning and swimming in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> in the afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-Aikman2009_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aikman2009-247">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> At the competitive level, basketball and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> are among Lebanon's most popular sports. <a href="/wiki/Canoeing" title="Canoeing">Canoeing</a>, cycling, <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">rafting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climbing" title="Climbing">climbing</a>, swimming, sailing and <a href="/wiki/Caving" title="Caving">caving</a> are among the other common leisure sports in Lebanon. The <a href="/wiki/Beirut_Marathon" title="Beirut Marathon">Beirut Marathon</a> is held every fall, drawing top runners from Lebanon and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_in_Lebanon" title="Rugby league in Lebanon">Rugby league</a> is a relatively new but growing sport in Lebanon. The <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_national_rugby_league_team" title="Lebanon national rugby league team">Lebanon national rugby league team</a> participated in the <a href="/wiki/2000_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2000 Rugby League World Cup">2000 Rugby League World Cup</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> and narrowly missed qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008</a><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013</a> tournaments.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon also took part in the <a href="/wiki/2009_European_Cup" title="2009 European Cup">2009 European Cup</a> where, after narrowly failing to qualify for the final, the team defeated <a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_league_team" title="Ireland national rugby league team">Ireland</a> to finish 3rd in the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hazem_El_Masri" title="Hazem El Masri">Hazem El Masri</a>, who was born in Tripoli, will always be considered to be the greatest <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a> to ever play the game. He immigrated to <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> from Lebanon in 1988. He became the greatest point-scorer in <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> history in 2009 by scoring himself 2418 points while playing for Australian club, <a href="/wiki/Canterbury-Bankstown_Bulldogs" title="Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs">Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs</a> where he also holds the record for most first grade appearances for the club with 317 games and most tries for the club with 159 tries. At international level, He also hold the records as top-try scorer with 12 tries and top-point scorer with 136 points for the Lebanese national team.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanon participates in <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">Basketball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_national_basketball_team" title="Lebanon national basketball team">Lebanese National Team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIBA_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA World Championship">FIBA World Championship</a> 3 times in a row.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Dominant Basketball teams in Lebanon are <a href="/wiki/Sporting_Al_Riyadi_Beirut" title="Sporting Al Riyadi Beirut">Sporting Al Riyadi Beirut</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> who are the current Arab and Asian champions, <a href="/wiki/Hekmeh" class="mw-redirect" title="Hekmeh">Club Sagesse</a> who were able to earn the Asian and Arab championships before. <a href="/wiki/Fadi_El_Khatib" title="Fadi El Khatib">Fadi El Khatib</a> is the most decorated player in the Lebanese National Basketball League.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Lebanon" title="Football in Lebanon">Football</a> is also one of the more popular sports in the country with the <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Premier_League" title="Lebanese Premier League">Lebanese Premier League</a>, whose most successful clubs are the <a href="/wiki/Al-Ansar_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Ansar Club">Al-Ansar Club</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nejmeh_SC" title="Nejmeh SC">Nejmeh SC</a>, with notable players being <a href="/wiki/Roda_Antar" title="Roda Antar">Roda Antar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Youssef_Mohamad" title="Youssef Mohamad">Youssef Mohamad</a>, the first Arab to captain a European premier league team.
</p><p>In recent years, Lebanon has hosted the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Pan_Arab_Games" title="Pan Arab Games">Pan Arab Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> Lebanon hosted the <a href="/wiki/2009_Jeux_de_la_Francophonie" title="2009 Jeux de la Francophonie">2009 Jeux de la Francophonie</a><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> from 27 September to 6 October, and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon_at_the_Olympics" title="Lebanon at the Olympics">have participated</a> in every <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since its independence, winning a total of four medals.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Prominent Lebanese bodybuilders include <a href="/wiki/Samir_Bannout" title="Samir Bannout">Samir Bannout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Bannout" title="Mohammad Bannout">Mohammad Bannout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Haidar" title="Ahmad Haidar">Ahmad Haidar</a>.
</p><p>Water sports have also shown to be very active in the past years, in Lebanon. Since 2012 and with the emergence of the Lebanon Water Festival NGO, more emphasis has been placed on those sports, and Lebanon has been pushed forward as a water sport destination internationally.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> They host different contests and water show sports that encourage their fans to participate and win big.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Lebanon" title="Education in Lebanon">Education in Lebanon</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/180px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/270px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg/360px-Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Universitet_Haigazian.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haigazian_University" title="Haigazian University">Haigazian University</a> in Beirut.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AUB_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/AUB_1.jpg/180px-AUB_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/AUB_1.jpg/270px-AUB_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/AUB_1.jpg/360px-AUB_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AUB_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">AUB</a> College Hall in Beirut.</div></div></div>
<p>Listed by the World Economic Forum's 2013 Global Information Technology Report, Lebanon has been ranked globally as the fourth best country for math and science education, and as the tenth best overall for quality of education. In quality of management schools, the country was ranked 13th worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The United Nations assigned Lebanon an education index of 0.871 in 2008. The index, which is determined by the adult literacy rate and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary gross enrollment ratio, ranked the country 88th out of the 177 countries participating.<sup id="cite_ref-undp_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-undp-265">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All Lebanese schools are required to follow a prescribed curriculum designed by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_and_Higher_Education_(Lebanon)" title="Ministry of Education and Higher Education (Lebanon)">Ministry of Education</a>. Some of the 1400 private schools offer <a href="/wiki/IB_program" class="mw-redirect" title="IB program">IB programs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> and may also add more courses to their curriculum with approval from the Ministry of Education. The first eight years of education are, by law, compulsory.<sup id="cite_ref-dos-2010-03-22_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dos-2010-03-22-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lebanon has forty-one nationally accredited universities, several of which are internationally recognized.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">American University of Beirut</a> (AUB) and the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Saint-Joseph" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Saint-Joseph">Université Saint-Joseph</a> (USJ) were the first Anglophone and the first Francophone universities to open in Lebanon, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Universities in Lebanon, both public and private, largely operate in French or English.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The top-ranking universities in the country are the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Beirut" title="American University of Beirut">American University of Beirut</a> (#237 worldwide, #2 in the Middle East as of 2019),<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_American_University" title="Lebanese American University">Lebanese American University</a> (#580s worldwide as of 2019),<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Saint_Joseph_de_Beyrouth" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Saint Joseph de Beyrouth">Université Saint Joseph de Beyrouth</a> (#500 worldwide as of 2019),<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Libanaise" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Libanaise">Université Libanaise</a> (#3,826 worldwide) and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit_University_of_Kaslik" title="Holy Spirit University of Kaslik">Holy Spirit University of Kaslik</a> (#600s worldwide as of 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Lebanon" title="Health in Lebanon">Health in Lebanon</a></div>
<p>In 2010, spending on healthcare accounted for 7.03% of the country's GDP. In 2009, there were 31.29 physicians and 19.71 nurses per 10,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> The life expectancy at birth was 72.59 years in 2011, or 70.48 years for males and 74.80 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the end of the civil war, only one third of the country's public hospitals were operational, each with an average of only 20 beds. By 2009 the country had 28
public hospitals, with a total of 2,550 beds.<sup id="cite_ref-healthref_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healthref-278">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> At public hospitals, hospitalized uninsured patients pay 5% of the bill, in comparison with 15% in private hospitals, with the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://moph.gov.lb/en">Ministry of Public Health</a> reimbursing the remainder.<sup id="cite_ref-healthref_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-healthref-278">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> The Ministry of Public Health contracts with 138 private hospitals and 25 public hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-statbul11_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbul11-279">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, there were 236,643 subsidized admissions to hospitals; 164,244 in private hospitals, and 72,399 in public hospitals. More patients visit private hospitals than public hospitals, because the private beds supply is higher.<sup id="cite_ref-statbul11_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statbul11-279">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recently, there has been an increase in foodborne illnesses which has put an emphasis on the importance of the safety of the food chain in Lebanon. This raised the illues public awareness. More restaurants are seeking information and compliance with <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kebabs_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kebabs-280">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lebanon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Article 11 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Lebanon" title="Constitution of Lebanon">Constitution of Lebanon</a> states: "Arabic is the official national language. A law shall determine the cases in which the French language can be used." See: <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Lebanon" title="French language in Lebanon">French language in Lebanon</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Also called Lebanese, it is the daily spoken language of the vast majority of the local population, with a romanized written form used in informal communications. It is significantly influenced by Aramaic, Syriac, as well as other languages.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Republic of Lebanon</i> is the most common phrase used by Lebanese government agencies. The phrase <i>Lebanese Republic</i> is a literal translation of the official <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> names, no longer in use. <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Arabic" title="Lebanese Arabic">Lebanese Arabic</a> is the most common language spoken by the citizens of Lebanon.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Excluding the partially-recognized <i><a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">State of Palestine</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a>, whilst all smaller than Lebanon and considered parts of Asia, are entirely on islands, and therefore off the Asian continental mass.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-67">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2005: <a href="/wiki/Bassel_Fleihan" title="Bassel Fleihan">Bassel Fleihan</a>, Lebanese legislator and Minister of Economy and Commerce; <a href="/wiki/Samir_Kassir" title="Samir Kassir">Samir Kassir</a>, Columnist and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Left_Movement_(Lebanon)" title="Democratic Left Movement (Lebanon)">Democratic Left Movement</a> leader; <a href="/wiki/George_Hawi" title="George Hawi">George Hawi</a>, former head of <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Communist_Party" title="Lebanese Communist Party">Lebanese Communist Party</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gibran_Tueni" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibran Tueni">Gibran Tueni</a>, Editor in Chief of "An Nahar" newspaper. 2006: <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Gemayel" title="Pierre Gemayel">Pierre Gemayel</a>, Minister of Industry. 2007: <a href="/wiki/Walid_Eido" title="Walid Eido">Walid Eido</a>, MP; <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Ghanim" class="mw-redirect" title="Antoine Ghanim">Antoine Ghanim</a>, MP.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-Firro2003-37"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Firro2003_37-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Firro, Kais (8 February 2003). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=zRwOcE9wJAQC&amp;pg=PA18"><i>Inventing Lebanon: Nationalism and the State Under the Mandate</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-Rooke-38"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Rooke_38-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Tetz Rooke (2013). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ykTYAQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA178">"Writing the Boundary: "Khitat al-Shăm" by Muhammad Kurd ʹAli"</a>.  In Hiroyuki (ed.). <i>Concept Of Territory In Islamic Thought</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;178. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-136-18453-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-136-18453-6"><bdi>978-1-136-18453-6</bdi></a>. <q>His [(<a href="/wiki/Thongchai_Winichakul" title="Thongchai Winichakul">Thongchai Winichakul</a>’s)] study shows that the modern map in some cases predicted the nation instead of just recording it; rather than describing existing borders it created the reality it was assumed to depict. The power of the map over the mind was great:"[H]ow could a nation resist being found if a nineteenth-century map had predicted it?" In the Middle East, Lebanon seems to offer a corresponding example. When the idea of a Greater Lebanon in 1908 was put forward in a book by Bulus Nujaym, a Lebanese Maronite writing under the pseudonym of M. Jouplain, he suggested that the natural boundaries of Lebanon were exactly the same as drawn in the 1861 and 1863 staff maps of the French military expedition to Syria, maps that added territories on the northern, eastern and southern borders, plus the city of Beirut, to the Mutasarrifiyya of Mount Lebanon. In this case, too, the prior existence of a European military map seems to have created a fact on the ground.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Writing+the+Boundary%3A+%22Khitat+al-Sh%C4%83m%22+by+Muhammad+Kurd+%CA%B9Ali&amp;rft.btitle=Concept+Of+Territory+In+Islamic+Thought&amp;rft.pages=178&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-136-18453-6&amp;rft.au=Tetz+Rooke&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DykTYAQAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA178&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALebanon" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Gorton, T.J. (25 April 2013). <i>Renaissance Emir</i>. Quartet Books. pp.&#160;160–161. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780704372979" title="Special:BookSources/9780704372979"><bdi>9780704372979</bdi></a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Renaissance+Emir&amp;rft.pages=160-161&amp;rft.pub=Quartet+Books&amp;rft.date=2013-04-25&amp;rft.isbn=9780704372979&amp;rft.au=Gorton%2C+T.J.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALebanon" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
